None Shanghai , May 9 ( XINHUA ) --####[]
None The spreading AIDS epidemic is threatening Asia 's economic growth , warned officials from the United Nations Program on HIV / AIDS ( UNAIDS ) , the World Health Organization and bank delegates at " Investing in Asia 's Health " , an Asian Development Bank ( ADB ) seminar held here Thursday .####[([1, 5], [11, 12], [12, 51], 'Negative', 'Strong'), ([1, 11], [11, 12], [12, 51], 'Negative', 'Strong')]
None Statistics show that about two people in the Asia-Pacific region are infected every minute , and a total of over one million people were infected in 2001 .####[]
None " AIDS is casting shadow on Asia 's economic miracle , and is turning into a global crisis , as the region accounts for 60 percent of world 's population , " says Michel Sidibe , Director of the Country and Regional Support Department of UNAIDS .####[]
None Research newly released by the WHO indicates that societies with a heavy burden of disease tend to experience a multiplicity of severe impediments to economic progress especially to sustainable economic growth .####[]
None It suggests that each 10 percent improvement in life expectancy at birth is associated with a rise in economic growth of at least 0.3 to 0.4 percent per year .####[]
None " With an alarming infection growth rate in many Asian Pacific countries , care for AIDS is over- burdening the health care system and is taking away from provision of other health services , " said Sidibe .####[]
None In countries such as China and India where AIDS was still at an early phase of the AIDS pandemic , timely control measures were critical to head off an explosive growth in infection , but these demanded heavy expenditure , he said .####[]
None Jeffrey Sachs , director for the Center for International Development at Harvard University and chairman of the WHO Commission on Macroeconomics and Health , believes developing countries should fully recognize the importance of investing in health in their overall development strategy .####[]
None In his report , " Macroeconomics and Health : Investing in Health for Economic Development " , released by the WHO last December , Sachs estimated that total annual health outlays in world 's least - developed countries would rise by 17 billion U.S. dollars by 2007 and 29 billion U.S. dollars by 2015 and AIDS prevention and care would account for half the increase .####[]
None However , low-income countries would be able to pay 14 billion U. S. dollars and 21 billion U.S. dollars respectively at best , said Sachs .####[]
None The WHO 's recommendations for each developing country include increasing investment in health and relevant areas like education , water and agricultural development ; the establishing of a temporary National Commission on Macroeconomics and Health ( NCMH ) , chaired jointly by the Ministers of Health and Finance to organize and lead the medical as well as economic war against AIDS and other diseases .####[]
None Sachs also addressed the exacerbating condition of the AIDS pandemic in China , saying that China had the technical ability to control AIDS infection , but still needed a comprehensive strategy , including local surveillance network , increasing government subsidiary and free medicine for the poor .####[([8, 13], [2, 4], [1, 2], 'Neutral', 'Weak')]

None Guantanamo to hold terror prisoners####[]
None The U.S. naval base at Guantamano Bay , Cuba , once a detention center for thousands of Cubans and Haitians seeking freedom in America , may soon become a prison for men with a radically different view of the country .####[([39, 41], [34, 38], [32, 33], 'Neutral', 'Strong'), ([21, 25], [20, 21], [17, 20], 'Positive', 'Weak')]
None The Pentagon is planning to house captured al Qaeda terrorists and Taliban fighters for an undetermined time at the base on the island 's isolated eastern coast , Defense Secretary Donald Rumsfeld said Thursday .####[]

None U.S. Rep. Ileana Ros-Lehtinen , R- Miami , said she supported the idea , in part , because it would underscore the naval base 's strategic importance at a time when some members of Congress have urged returning the territory to Cuba .####[([37, 43], [36, 37], [32, 36], 'Positive', 'Average'), ([12, 15], [10, 12], [1, 6], 'Positive', 'Weak')]

None U.S. officials began using it as an offshore holding station during a Haitian refugee crisis in 1991 .####[]
None During the 1994 - 95 rafter crisis , 50,000 Cubans and Haitians were housed there in a tent encampment after U.S. naval vessels had picked them up at sea .####[]

None Others are at a U.S. military compound in Kandahar , Afghanistan , where U.S. forces built a stockade of sorts to house them .####[]

None With an outdoor movie theater , bowling alleys , a McDonald 's and a mini-mall , Guantanamo Bay is a curious slice of Americana on the edge of the Caribbean .####[]

None No updated figure was available Thursday .####[]
None The base is extremely isolated .####[]
None Visitors can reach it only under strict military escort and with prior permission from the Pentagon , aboard special small shuttle flights that reach the base by a circuitous flight from the United States .####[]
None On rare occasions , Cuban defectors get there by swimming through dangerous waters or by traversing a Cuban minefield .####[]
None There is also a gate between Cuba proper and the base that is sometimes opened for meetings between military commanders , or to repatriate Cubans who have been taken to the base .####[]
None Cuban leader Fidel Castro has long argued that the U.S. military occupation of the base is illegal , while U.S. officials say the base exists under a lease agreement that was part of a 1934 treaty with Cuba .####[]

None The government is sharpening its newest weapon against white -collar defendants : the power to prevent them from paying their legal bills .####[]
None And defense lawyers are warning that they wo n't stick around if they do n't get paid .####[]
None The issue has come to a boil in Newark , N.J. , where federal prosecutors have warned lawyers for Eddie Antar that if the founder and former chairman of Crazy Eddie Inc. is indicted , the government may move to seize the money that Mr. Antar is using to pay legal fees .####[]
None The warning by the U.S. attorney 's office follows two decisions by the U.S. Supreme Court last June .####[]
None In those cases , the high court ruled that federal law gives prosecutors broad authority to seize assets of people accused of racketeering and drug-related crimes , including fees paid to lawyers before an indictment .####[]
None If the government succeeds in seizing Mr. Antar 's assets , he could be left without top-flight legal representation , because his attorneys are likely to quit , according to individuals familiar with the case .####[]
None A seizure also would make the case the largest -- and one of the first -- in which lawyers ' fees have been confiscated in a prosecution unrelated to drugs .####[]
None " The people who suffer in the short run are defendants , but the people who suffer in the long run are all of the people , because there wo n't be a vigorous private bar to defend the Bill of Rights , " says Gerald Lefcourt , a criminal defense attorney who says he has turned down a number of cases to avoid possible fee seizures .####[]
None Mr. Antar is being investigated by a federal grand jury in Newark , where prosecutors have told him that they may soon seek an indictment on racketeering and securities fraud charges .####[]
None Under the Racketeer Influenced and Corrupt Organizations law , or RICO , the government has the authority to seek to freeze or seize a defendant 's assets before trial .####[]
None According to individuals familiar with Mr. Antar 's case , prosecutors issued their warning this week after one of Mr. Antar 's attorneys asked whether legal fees might be subject to seizure .####[]
None In a letter , prosecutors told Mr. Antar 's lawyers that because of the recent Supreme Court rulings , they could expect that any fees collected from Mr. Antar may be seized .####[]
None Prosecutors have told Mr. Antar 's attorneys that they believe Mr. Antar 's allegedly ill-gotten gains are so great that any money he has used to pay attorneys derives from illegal activities .####[]
None Therefore , they said , the money can be taken from the lawyers even after they are paid .####[]
None Justin Feldman and Jack Arseneault , attorneys for Mr. Antar , both declined to comment on the matter .####[]
None In Newark , U.S. Attorney Samuel A. Alito said , " I do n't think there 's any legal reason to limit forfeiture of attorney 's fees to drug cases . "####[]
None Mr. Alito said his office " just responded to an attorney 's question about whether we would go after attorney 's fees , and that is different from actually doing it , although we reserve that right . "####[]
None Mr. Antar was charged last month in a civil suit filed in federal court in Newark by the Securities and Exchange Commission .####[]
None In that suit , the SEC accused Mr. Antar of engaging in a " massive financial fraud " to overstate the earnings of Crazy Eddie , Edison , N.J. , over a three - year period .####[]
None Through his lawyers , Mr. Antar has denied allegations in the SEC suit and in civil suits previously filed by shareholders against Mr. Antar and others .####[]
None The SEC has alleged that Mr. Antar aimed to pump up the company 's stock price through false financial statements in order to sell his stake and reap huge profits .####[]
None Mr. Antar , the SEC said , made more than $ 60 million from the sale of his shares between 1985 and 1987 .####[]
None The Justice Department has emphasized that the government 's fee-forfeiture power is to be used sparingly .####[]
None According to department policy , prosecutors must make a strong showing that lawyers ' fees came from assets tainted by illegal profits before any attempts at seizure are made .####[]
None Still , criminal defense lawyers worry that defendants are being deprived of their Sixth Amendment right to counsel and a fair trial if the government can seize lawyers ' fees .####[]
None They also worry that if the government applies asset-forfeiture laws broadly , the best defense lawyers will be unwilling to take criminal cases unless they are assured of being paid .####[]

None Tokyo irked by US stance on Kyoto####[([4, 7], [2, 3], [1], 'Negative', 'Average')]
None TOKYO - Coral reefs will die from water that 's too hot .####[]
None Polar bears will have less room to roam , crowding some of them out of existence .####[]
None Birds will start flying an extra mile north each year , and may starve when they get there .####[]
None These are among the dire possible consequences of global warming , say climate - change experts .####[]
None At no time was it clearer that countries should take steps to slow this process than when 150 countries signed the Kyoto Protocol in 1997 .####[]
None But now , with President George Bush saying the US will not ratify the protocol - which was shaped in part to fit Washington 's concerns five years ago - the accord 's ultimate effectiveness is in doubt , and many US allies are irritated .####[([9, 16], [44, 46], [41, 44], 'Negative', 'Average'), ([0], [25, 27], [23, 25], 'Negative', 'Average')]

None The clash over how to stop global warming while allowing sluggish economies to prosper occurs at an awkward point in US - Japanese relations .####[]

None Endeavour Shuttle To Return On Monday####[]
None The Endeavour shuttle is expected to land on the US Cape Canaveral launch site , Florida , at 08:55 p. m. , Moscow time , the Russian Mission Control reported .####[]
None The shuttle will bring back to the Earth its crew , which has spent 7 days on - board the International Space Station ( ISS , ) and the 3rd long-term expedition to the ISS , namely , American astronaut Frank Culbertson and two Russian cosmonauts Vladimir Dezhurov and Mikhail Tyurin .####[]
None Back on the Earth , they will report about the results they have obtained since August 13 .####[]
None The primary objective of the shuttle 's mission to the ISS was to deliver the 4th ISS crew and research equipment .####[]
None According to the Mission Control , the shuttle 's crew has perfectly accomplished its mission .####[]
None On its way home , the shuttle launched into space the Starshine micro-satellite , which had been designed by students .####[]
None According to the Mission Control , the satellite which is no larger than a volley ball , has been made by thousands of students who were polishing small pieces of glass subsequently putting them on its surface .####[]
None It slightly resembles of these rotating glass balls which are usually used in disco clubs .####[]
None It is believed that the glass will make it possible to see the satellite at night .####[]
None Students of several universities , in their turn , will be calculating its speed and its orbit parameters .####[]
None The 4th long-term expedition to the ISS is led by Russian cosmonaut Yuri Onufriyenko .####[]
None There are two US astronauts under his command - Carl Waltz and Daniel Bursch .####[]
None This crew will stay on - board the ISS till May 2002 .####[]

None Why Kyoto is a rip-off####[]
None According to a study released last week by the Canadian Manufacturers and Exporters , implementation of the 1997 Kyoto global warming treaty would cost our economy 450,000 jobs and as much as $ 40 - billion .####[]
None But Jean Chretien is not worried .####[([0], [4, 7], [2, 4], 'Neutral', 'Average')]
None " I do n't accept these figures , " the Prime Minister said .####[]
None " There is nothing to be gained by frightening people when all the facts are not known . "####[([0], [8, 9], [0], 'Negative', 'Strong')]
None But the $ 40 - billion figure , far from being conceived to " frighten " Canadians , is plucked straight from government documents .####[([3, 8], [14, 16], [16, 19], 'Negative', 'Strong')]
None According to a report released in 2000 by the National Air Issues Co-ordinating Committee on Climate Change , a group staffed by officials from the federal , provincial and territorial governments , hitting Canada 's Kyoto target may mean " the loss of roughly one year 's growth , or , viewed in absolute terms , in 2010 , the loss in annual economic output of approximately $ 40 - billion ( or $ 1,100 per capita ) . "####[]
None This is not a price worth paying .####[]
None Governments are expected to protect the national economy , and they should deviate from that mission only when crucial national interests are at stake ( fighting terrorism , for example ) .####[]
None Yet rising temperatures pose little threat to Canada .####[]
None In its authoritative Feb. , 2001 , report on the projected impacts of global warming , the Intergovernmental Panel on Climate Change identified several threats to Canadian ecosystems , but concluded that our farmers would generally benefit from warmer temperatures .####[]
None ( Non-farming Canadians , most of whom spend at least part of the winter months scraping ice off their cars , chopping firewood and shovelling their walks , will profit as well . )####[]
None As for the globally felt benefits that would follow from Canada 's implementation of the Kyoto protocol , they are slight .####[]
None By 2010 , our $ 40 - billion sacrifice would yield an expected reduction in annual carbon and carbon - equivalent emissions of about 46 - million tonnes -- just 1/200th of the world 's total projected greenhouse gas output .####[]
None Even if Canada managed to convince the United States and every other Kyoto signatory to ratify the protocol , world carbon dioxide emissions would still soar .####[]
None According to the U.S. Energy Information Administration , world energy consumption will increase by about 60 % between now and 2020 , with most of the upsurge expected to come from developing nations , which are not covered by the Kyoto Protocol .####[]
None Under the fully implemented treaty , carbon dioxide emissions would grow 26 % during the 1990 - 2010 period .####[]
None Without Kyoto , the figure would be 34 % .####[]
None The worldwide cost of that 8 % dip : about $ 2 - trillion in lost GDP -- give or take a trillion .####[]
None There are better ways to spend that money .####[]
None Instead of trying to cap carbon dioxide emissions -- a costly burden at home and an impossible task in the developing world -- we should focus on abating the damage global warming does in at-risk nations .####[]
None If scientists are correct , higher temperatures and rising sea levels will depress grain yields in Africa and parts of Asia , fuel the spread of diseases , and threaten coastal nations such as Bangladesh and Senegal .####[]
None But these problems can be abated , or even eliminated , with Western assistance .####[]
None While helping Third World nations plant new crops , vaccinate people and relocate coastal towns will be costly , the bottom line will likely be only a fraction of Kyoto 's 13 - digit price tag .####[]

None The businessman , who identified himself as Ivan Ivanov and has worked in India , Pakistan , Sri Lanka and the United Arab Emirates , told AFP that a group of Pakistani nationals introduced him to bin Laden , the prime suspect in the US terrorist attacks , on April 10 in Peshawar .####[]
None A young Arab chemical engineer contacted him the next day , he said , to ask him to act as an intermediary in the sale of the nuclear fuel from the Kozlodui nuclear power plant .####[([17, 36], [15, 17], [1, 5], 'Positive', 'Weak')]
None The businessman said he turned down an offer of a 200,000 dollar commission for the sale .####[]
None The head of the nuclear energy department at Bulgaria 's energy agency separately said he could not imagine a terrorist organisation making a bomb out of products from the reactors at the Kozlodui power station .####[]

None They are stockpiled in a secure depot located inside the power station before being sent to Russia to be processed , " said Anton Ivanov .####[]
None Researchers from the Weizmann Institute in Rehovot and the Technion in Haifa have developed a computer so tiny that a trillion of them could fit into a laboratory test tube .####[]
None The " computers " are biological molecules , using DNA for software and enzymes for hardware , and can solve a billion mathematical problems a second .####[]
None Such tiny devices could one day fit into cells and supervise biological processes , or even synthesize drugs .####[]
None DNA strands exist in almost every body cell -- they are biological software that tell each cell and molecule what to do .####[]
None " If you look at the mechanism of a cell , a lot of what goes on inside is computation .####[]
None We do n't need to teach the cell new tricks , we just need to put the existing tricks in the right order , " says Prof .####[]
None Ehud Shapiro of the Weizmann Institute , who headed the research .####[]
None Some scientists believe DNA - based computers could have an advantage over existing computers based on silicon chips .####[]
None Artificial chips have reached their limits and ca n't get any smaller .####[]
None But , say the scientists , tiny DNA strands can store huge amounts of information in minuscule space -- one cubic centimeter of DNA can store more information than a trillion CDs .####[]
None Prof .####[]
None Shapiro says the molecular computer is the first of its kind .####[]
None Although computers with DNA input and output have been made before , they have always involved a laborious series of reactions , each requiring human supervision .####[]
None " Previous biological computers were the same size as the room in which the supervisors and computer equipment worked , " said Shapiro .####[]
None " With the new method , all you need do to get an answer is put all the ingredients into a test tube , mix them together , and check to see what the output is . "####[]
None For now biological computers only know how to answer simple questions with a " yes " or " no " response .####[]
None A typical question would be :####[]
None In the sequence " AAB " is there an equal number of As and Bs ?####[]
None Nevertheless , several researchers worldwide have hailed the computers as an important new development .####[([8, 10], [6, 8], [2, 6], 'Positive', 'Strong')]
None " They work better than anything I 've seen so far , " said Eric Baum , a computer scientist at the NEC Research Institute in Princeton , New Jersey .####[]
None Although he questions whether biomolecular computers will ever become really useful , he believes they are a " step in the right direction . "####[([15, 16], [13, 15], [13], 'Neutral', 'Average')]
None Professor Shapiro and a growing number of other scientists believe DNA - based computers may lead to a number of useful applications -- they could be planted inside cells , where they would watch for irregularities or even synthesize drugs .####[]
None The computer simulates the cell 's natural mechanisms with an accuracy level of 99.8 percent .####[]
None Natural DNA processes also involve inaccuracies which are corrected by other genes , says Shapiro , and it is almost impossible to reach absolute accuracy using biological systems .####[]
None However , for the uses for which the computers are designated , this level of accuracy is adequate .####[]
None So how does such a computer work ?####[]
None Let 's say the computer wants to know whether the number of times a " B " DNA type appears in a DNA section is odd or even .####[]
None The DNA section -- the " input " -- is inserted into a chemical solution along with enzymes to be used as the computer 's " hardware " .####[]
None Other DNA sections are added , which act as " software " .####[]
None A software section sticks to the input with the help of an enzyme .####[]
None If the tip of the input is " B " , the input will be labeled as having an odd number of " B " sequences .####[]
None Another enzyme then cuts the section and reveals the next sequence .####[]
None Each time " B " appears , the label on the input changes from " even " to " odd " and back again .####[]
None Once the computer has dissected the entire input , it can determine whether the sequence appeared an even or odd number of times according to the last label -- the " output " .####[]
None The computer can also do other calculations , such as checking whether the " B " sequence appears at least once , or at most once , by inserting different types of software DNAs .####[]

None Achieving this would only be a first step towards stabilising global greenhouse gas concentrations at a level that would prevent dangerous climate change .####[]
None This is the ultimate objective of the Convention to which the US has subscribed .####[]
None However , the new plan does not lead to such a stabilisation , but instead will lead to the increase of absolute emission levels .####[]
None Over the past years , greenhouse gas emissions intensity in relation to GDP has been falling in the US .####[]
None The Bush plan is based on a prolongation of this trend thereby in effect foreseeing little more than continuation on a " business - as-usual " path .####[]
None Current emission projections for the US indicate an increase of 39 % above 1990 levels in 2012 .####[]
None While the intensity improvements may reduce this to around 33 % , this is still a very substantial increase in absolute emissions .####[]
None The EU is concerned about the purely voluntary nature of the actions proposed .####[([6, 14], [3, 4], [1, 3], 'Negative', 'Average')]
None Furthermore , a review of the effectiveness of the measures will not take place before 2012 .####[]
None It is striking that the approach which is considered beneficial for other air pollutants , namely to implement cap-and - trade programmes , is not extended to CO2 emissions from the power sector .####[]
None The EU is of the opinion that a cap-and - trade system is a cost-effective measure to reduce emissions which combines a guaranteed environmental result with the flexibility to reduce emissions where it is least costly .####[]
None By 2005 , the EU intends to implement a cap-and - trade system covering 46 % of all CO2 emissions in 2010 .####[]
None The EU welcomes the fact that the Bush administration has now completed its policy review and has put forward what the US intends to do in terms of domestic climate change policy .####[([4, 33], [2, 4], [1, 2], 'Positive', 'Average')]
None The proposals by President Bush may represent a first step in the right direction , where also economic operators in the US are asked to contribute to emission control .####[]
None However , mandatory monitoring and reporting of emissions at company level would be necessary to adequately assess whether the proposals by President Bush represent an effort comparable to the ones under the Kyoto Protocol .####[]

None Mudede said on state television that Mugabe was re-elected with 1,685,212 votes against 1,258,758 votes for opposition challenger Morgan Tsvangirai .####[]
None " I ... therefore declare Robert Mugabe the winner for the office of the presidency of Zimbabwe , " Mudede said .####[]
None Mugabe passed the 50 per cent mark with only six districts left to be declared , official figures showed on Wednesday .####[]
None Results broadcast on state television gave Mugabe 1,634,382 votes , or 52 per cent of the 3.1 million ballots cast .####[]
None His main rival Morgan Tsvangirai of the Movement for Democratic Change ( MDC ) had 1,185,890 votes , or 38 per cent of the votes cast .####[]
None Tsvangirai , along with local and international observers , have cited widespread abuses in the electoral process .####[]
None The MDC leadership was to meet mid-morning to discuss the results .####[]
None " We have a national executive meeting ... where we will be looking at the figures and give the reaction of the party , " said David Coltart , MP for the Movement for Democratic Change ( Mdc ) .####[]
None " To put it mildly the figures are very odd , with very low turnouts in the cities and massives ones in the rural areas , which is unprecedented in this country , " he said .####[]
None Tsvangirai was due to address the media after the meeting , around noon ( 1000 GMT ) .####[]
None Meanwhile , about 100 soldiers surrounded the offices of the opposition Movement in Bulawayo on Wednesday , a reporter said .####[]

None CAPE CANAVERAL -- ( AP ) --####[]
None Two American astronauts and one Russian cosmonaut moved into the International Space Station on Saturday , settling in for a half - year stay .####[]
None The three men arrived aboard space shuttle Endeavour the day before , but did not have time to trade places with the space station crew that has been on board since August .####[]
None The new residents ' form-fitting seat liners for the lifeboat had to be carried over and installed , and their space suits tucked away , before they could call space station Alpha home .####[]
None Russian Yuri Onufrienko could n't wait to take over as space station commander from American Frank Culbertson .####[([7, 18], [4, 7], [0, 3], 'Positive', 'Strong')]
None The cosmonaut kept peeking through a small window before the hatch finally swung open between the docked spacecraft .####[]
None Onufrienko will remain on board until May , along with astronauts Daniel Bursch and Carl Walz .####[]
None As gear moved back and forth across the threshold , Endeavour 's astronauts used the ship 's robot arm to lift an Italian - built cargo carrier from the shuttle and attach it to the station .####[]
None The carrier , named Raffaello , is loaded with three tons of food , clothes , science experiments and spare parts .####[]
None Once emptied , it will be filled with dirty laundry , trash and used equipment and put back on Endeavour for the ride home .####[]
None The space station 's new residents also packed some personal items , reflecting their hobbies .####[]
None Onufrienko , a fisherman , took material to tie flies .####[]
None Bursch has weaving material to make small baskets , while Walz has a five-octave keyboard that he calls a ``psychological support device . ''####[]
None By the time Culbertson and his Russian crew mates , Mikhail Tyurin and Vladimir Dezhurov , return to Earth in another week , they will have spent 128 days in space .####[]

None Navy Officer Balances Religious Responsibilities####[]
None Miami Herald January 31 , 2002 Navy Officer Balances Religious Responsibilities By Carol Rosenberg####[]
None GUANTANAMO BAY NAVAL BASE , Cuba --####[]
None You 're the first-ever American Muslim cleric to minister to a prison camp full of suspected terrorists and one confides he has a weapon .####[]
None Do you keep the secret ?####[]
None Or do you breach religious confidentiality ?####[]
None If you 're U.S. Navy Lt. Abuhena Mohammad Saiful -Islam you search for a third way to resolve the clear conflict of interest between the crescent moon pin stuck in your left lapel and the lieutenant 's bars on the right side of your uniform .####[]
None ` ` I will say , ` Give it to me , ' -- and not tell the general who had it , '' he says softly but firmly .####[]
None ` ` I 'll make sure that he does n't have it . ''####[]
None A 39 - year- old life-long , practicing Muslim , the soft-spoken Bangladesh immigrant is navigating uncharted waters and juggling complicated loyalties -- all while managing an international spotlight he has never experienced before .####[]
None As a U.S. military chaplain , his contacts with prisoners are governed by the same confidentiality as that of a priest , minister or rabbi in the clergy corps .####[]
None Saiful -Islam is by training an imam , or a prayer leader , who guides the faithful in a mosque during the five-times - a- day Muslim prayer .####[]
None At Camp X-ray , he is also serving the function of a muezzin , the person who announces the call to prayer , commonly from a tower called a minaret .####[]
None In his case , he is using a public address system and recording the prayer for five-times - a- day broadcast .####[]
None Sometimes he laughs uncomfortably when questioned by journalists .####[([5, 9], [2, 5], [2], 'Negative', 'Average')]
None Sometimes he looks bewildered .####[]
None But mostly he 's a busy man , trying to soothe Muslim sensitivities over the rugged chain - linked - fence cells at Camp X-ray .####[]
None Advocate####[]
None Saiful -Islam arrived at the detention center for suspected terrorists on Jan. 24 and made his debut by chanting the pre-dawn call to prayer to wake up alleged leaders of Afghanistan 's Taliban militia and members of Osama bin Laden 's al Qaeda network .####[]
None Since then , he has emerged as their advocate , arguing that the U.S. military can safeguard its soldiers while adding a few amenities of everyday Islamic life .####[([0], [8, 10], [4, 5], 'Positive', 'Average')]
None Soon , he says , traditional white knit skullcaps will arrive for the captives to top off their fluorescent orange jumpsuits .####[]
None Saiful -Islam has also asked for some copies of the Koran , in Urdu , a language of Afghanistan and Pakistan , plus large-type , Arabic copies for those with bad eyesight or those who read like elementary school children .####[]
None ` ` These things are hard to find in America , and Gitmo is far , far away , '' says Saiful - Islam , a husband and father of a nearly 2 - year - old daughter in California .####[]
None Until he emerged as the chaplain of choice for this special assignment from among only 14 Muslim clerics in the U.S. armed forces , he was the only cleric specifically assigned to a Marine Corps base -- at Camp Pendleton , Calif .####[]
None Military recruiters building a Muslim chaplains corps spotted Saiful -Islam in 1993 , while he was an enlisted man working as a payroll clerk in the Pentagon and studying part-time to become a Muslim cleric .####[]
None He was commissioned as an officer in 1998 , just a year after obtaining U.S. citizenship and nine years after leaving his homeland to study in America .####[]
None The first time he was sent to a theater of combat came in October when he served as chaplain at Operation Brightstar , a huge military exercise in Egypt not far from the World War II battleground called al- Alamein .####[]
None No Answers####[]
None His role has a curious juxtaposition , which he sums up simply .####[]
None Captives at Camp X -ray are entitled to spiritual solace , he says , even though he does n't accept radical interpretations that have led them to an unorthodox battlefield against the so-called Great Satan , the United States .####[]
None ` `I , of course , do n't agree with their cause , '' he says , ``and neither does the religion , Islam . ''####[]
None But after several days of four - and five-hour shifts inside the camp , hearing the prisoners ' requests , he said exchanges have not dipped that deeply into the doctrinal .####[([0], [18, 21], [16, 18], 'Neutral', 'Weak')]
None Mostly , they ask about their fate , and when they might go home .####[]
None `` I do n't have any answer for them , '' he says .####[]
None Conversations between the cleric and the captives have taken place , one on one , in his native Bengali and Urdu .####[]
None Others require the services of Arabic interpreters -- who , like Saiful -Islam , are U.S. military men in battle dress uniforms .####[]
None So far no one has asked him how a practicing Muslim can also wear the uniform of the U.S. armed forces .####[]
None It was a question he had expected .####[]
None But instead , he says with surprise , ` ` They all want to speak with me .####[([11, 18], [5, 9], [4, 5], 'Neutral', 'Average'), ([15, 18], [13, 14], [4, 5], 'Positive', 'Average')]
None They all raise their hands ' ' to catch the attention of the U.S. government 's designated spiritual leader .####[]

None Announcing this at a news conference , Mr Sunil Mittal , Chairman &amp ; amp ; Managing Director , Bharti Enterprises , noted that the tariffs , which would be made available on its ILD [ international long distance ] services being launched on May 1 , would be revised downwards as and when the market demanded it .####[]
None " The present rate cut of up to 40 percent on peak -time rates is likely to be lowered after Videsh Sanchar Nigam Ltd ( VSNL ) and the other ILD operators , who are yet to begin services , announce their rates .####[]
None Unlike the STD [ subscriber trunk dialing ] services where a further rate cut may not be feasible , in the international services there is scope for more improvement , " he said .####[]

None Moscow , 5 May : Italian astronaut Roberto Vittori , a Russian cosmonaut and a paying space tourist , returned to earth today from their ten -day mission , including eight days aboard the International Space Station ( ISS ) .####[]
None " It was a tough but gratifying experience .####[]
None I 'm ready to go back , " Vittori told Italian general Mario Arpino during a telephone call shortly after the Russian Soyuz space capsule made its touch -down in Kazakhstan .####[]
None Russian officials said the three men , including the world 's second space tourist South African millionaire Mark Shuttleworth , were in fine condition .####[]
None Shuttleworth , 28 , who paid the Russians 20 m dollars for his jaunt in space , termed the experience " extraordinary . "####[]
None He became the world 's second space tourist , after US businessman Denis Tito made a similar voyage a year ago .####[]
None Vittori , 37 , spent eight months at Russia 's " Star City " in preparation for his 10 - day mission , dubbed Marco Polo by the Italian Space Agency .####[]

None His training in Russia combined with his knowledge of American techniques will put him at an advantage if the role of station commander should open up in the future , he said before his training started .####[]
None The role is currently reserved for Americans and Russians .####[]
None Italy 's Umberto Guidoni was the first European to set foot on board the ISS in April 2000 , while a third Italian astronaut , Paolo Nespoli , is scheduled to make his trip in 2003- 2004 .####[]
None The estimated cost of Vittori 's flight with the Russians was around 12.5 m dollars .####[]
None This covered his training , that of a Belgian substitute and the cost of carrying two scientific experiments on board the Russian Soyuz rocket .####[]

None The number of employees working on a temporary or daily basis have increased drastically as companies moved to slash labor costs after the financial crisis in 1997 , the National Statistical Office ( NSO ) said Friday .####[]
None NSO statistics showed that the number of workers employed on a temporary and daily basis rose by 888,000 to 6,962,000 in October compared with late 1997 .####[]
None The number working on a temporary basis went from 4,182,000 in late 1997 to 4,641,000 last month and that for those hired on a daily basis surged to 2,321,000 from 1,892,000 during the cited period .####[]
None The number of full-time workers declined 626,000 to 6,525,000 during the same time span .####[]
None " Demand for those working on a temporary or daily basis is risiing because companies are trying to save labor costs amid the continued economic slowdown , " an NSO official said .####[]
None Over 90 percent of full-time workers receive retirement allowances and bonuses but the comparable numbers fell to 10 percent for temporary workers and 1 percent for those employed on a daily basis .####[]
None About 80 to 90 percent of full-time workers were registered for the national pension , employment and health insurance systems while the comparable numbers shrank to 20 percent and 2 to 3 percent for temporary workers and those hired on a daily basis , respectively .####[]

None Even More " Proving Rape "####[]
None Chatterbox feels that the Wall Street Journal editorial page 's coverage of Juanita Broaddrick 's rape charges against Bill Clinton ( see " Proving Rape , " " More Proving Rape , " as well as Michael Kinsley 's " Readme " column in the current issue ) cries out for the introduction of the Scientific Method into the usually mushy business of assessing press responsibility .####[([4, 21], [2, 3], [0, 1], 'Neutral', 'Average')]
None With that in mind , Chatterbox hereby inaugurates the Intellectual Dishonesty ( henceforth to be known as the Indis ) Index .####[]
None Here 's how it works :####[]
None Publications that refuse to acknowledge ( even if to refute the importance of ) highly significant but inconvenient facts in their news or opinion coverage of controversial events will score one point for the initial offense .####[]
None They will then score one point for every subsequent issue or broadcast or Internet posting after the first offense is noted by Chatterbox if they continue not to report said inconvenient fact -- and an additional two points on days when the news organization runs a follow - up without making note of said inconvenient fact .####[([18, 20], [21, 22], [22, 24], 'Negative', None)]
None Publications receiving a score of 10 will be inducted into the Indis Hall of Fame .####[]
None Publications that get all the way up to 20 will be faxed a likeness of Joseph Stalin .####[]
None ( Chatterbox would prefer not to invoke the phrase " intellectual dishonesty , " because it 's pompous and falsely suggests that only intellectuals can be intellectually dishonest .####[([10, 14], [3, 14], [1, 2], 'Neutral', 'Average')]
None But Chatterbox does n't know any other easily understandable phrase that describes this particular kind of offense . )####[]
None For the purposes of this survey , the Wall Street Journal will be counted as a separate and distinct publication from the Journal 's editorial page , because , in essence , it is .####[]
None The Journal editorial page continues not to acknowledge that Norma Kelsey , the friend and employee to Juanita Broaddrick who is one of two people partially corroborating Broaddrick 's rape accusation , is the daughter of a man whose murderer was pardoned by Gov. Bill Clinton .####[]
None ( A responsible account of the whole controversy in today 's New York Times reports that Kelsey says the pardon had nothing to do with her corroboration . )####[]
None The Journal editorial page gets one point for failing to note the pardon in its initial Op - Ed by Dorothy Rabinowitz on Feb. 19 .####[]
None Because it has published three times since the initial omission , it scores an additional three points .####[]
None And because it published an editorial Feb. 22 taunting the rest of the press for not following it on the story -- and still did n't mention the pardon -- it scores an extra two points .####[]
None That comes to a total of six .####[]
None Chatterbox feels certain that the Journal editorial page will provide some follow - up tomorrow to tonight 's NBC broadcast of its own Broaddrick interview , which means that if the Journal editorial page continues to take no action it will be in the Indis Hall of Fame by Monday at the latest !####[]
None Chatterbox considered but rejected the idea of awarding Rabinowitz bonus points for having " eventually convinced " Broaddrick to grant an interview to the New York Times ( as the Times reports in today 's story ) .####[]
None But the Scientific Method does not permit any tinkering with the Indis Index 's scoring procedures .####[]
None And besides , Rabinowitz 's efforts on the Times ' behalf were n't really unethical , just puzzling , given the two newspapers ' intense rivalry .####[]
None When Chatterbox asked the Journal 's DC bureau chief , Alan Murray , who exercised good judgment in not breaking the Broaddrick story ( and - - full disclosure -- is Chatterbox 's former boss ) , to comment about a Journal employee 's feeding sources to the Times , he replied : " I do n't really have any comment on what the edit page did .####[]
None They do their thing , we do ours . "####[]
None Which is what Journal news employees are instructed to say whenever the editorial page causes them cringing embarrassment .####[]
None For her part , Rabinowitz explains to Chatterbox that her efforts on behalf of the Times were more indifferent than the Times made them sound .####[]
None " Ms. Broaddrick told me Sunday that a Times reporter had appeared at the house in the a.m. , and that she had refused an interview , " Rabinowitz writes in an e-mail message .####[]
None " I asked her why she had decided to talk to the New York Post 's Steve Dunleavy , and refused a Times reporter .####[]
None She said Dunleavy caught her by surprise .####[]
None She asked if I thought it would be all right to talk to the Times reporter .####[]
None I told her it would be -- certainly as all right as talking to Dunleavy .####[]
None She said , ' Well , I 'm sorry I did n't . '####[]
None She said she would if he called again .####[]
None I passed this on to [ Times reporter ] Felicity Barringer during our second day 's interview chat .####[]
None So -- that 's how it happens that in the New York Times piece today I 'm described -- solemnly -- as having ' eventually convinced ' her to repeat the story to the New York Times . "####[]

None Recent weeks have seen important developments on both sides of the Atlantic for the policy pursued in combating climate change .####[]
None In Europe , the council of environment ministers concluded a formal political agreement on 4 March on the decision to ratify the Kyoto Protocol before 1 June this year .####[]
None With this major decision , the European Union is opening the door to the entry into force of the Kyoto Protocol for climate protection just in time for the world summit on sustainable development to be held in August 2002 in Johannesburg .####[]
None In the United States , on 14 February President Bush presented the US national climate protection program .####[]
None It should be remembered that after Bush described the Kyoto Protocol as " fundamentally flawed " international negotiations on climate protection almost collapsed .####[]
None The United States , the world 's biggest emitter of greenhouse gases ( 25 percent of global emissions ) withdrew from an international agreement that , for the first time , set binding targets for developed countries for climate protection .####[]
None We now know that the US withdrawal did not stop the world community from deepening this important multilateral agreement for combating climate change .####[]
None The European Union played a dominant role in these negotiations and the community of states concluded , at the Bonn and Marrakech conferences of July and October last year , an agreement that sets out how to implement the Kyoto Protocol and provides for an original mechanism for respecting the reduction obligations that could possibly serve as a model for other agreements and that suggests a possible strengthening of international institutional structures in the environmental field .####[]
None This must now be ratified by all the parties and will shortly enter into force .####[]
None However , all the parties repeated with insistence that world climate protection cannot be effective unless the United States takes measures that are comparable to these taken by Europe and Japan .####[]
None Unfortunately , the recent US climate protection program falls far short of meeting such expectations .####[]
None Although there is a certain satisfaction at seeing President Bush recognize the need to fight climate change , that must not in any way conceal the extreme weakness of what he announced .####[]
None Under the US program , US emissions as a proportion of GDP must fall by 18 percent between 2002 and 2012 , or in other words energy efficiency must increase by 18 percent .####[]
None This can hardly be described as ambitious as a 15 percent increase in energy efficiency was in any event expected given present productivity levels .####[]
None In addition , if the US economy continues to grow , the increased energy efficiency will be cancelled out or more than cancelled out .####[]
None With an annual economic growth objective of 3 percent , absolute US emissions in 2012 will be 24.5 percent more than 1990 levels , despite the improvement in energy efficiency .####[]
None By comparison , respect for the Kyoto Protocol requires the EU to reduce its emissions by 8 percent compared with 1990 , Japan by 6 percent , and the United States by 7 percent , a figure accepted by President Clinton in 1997 .####[([6, 8], [3, 5], [0], 'Positive', 'Average')]
None The warnings by climate experts went unheeded in the US climate protection program .####[([0], [1, 3], [3, 6], 'Negative', 'Strong')]
None In its last report , the IPCC [ Intergovernmental Panel on Climate Change ] called for rapid and decisive action to at least avert the most serious consequences of climate change .####[([17, 21], [14, 16], [6, 8], 'Positive', 'Weak')]
None Scientists estimate that the industrialized countries must reduce their emissions to around 70 percent by 2020 to maintain climate change at an acceptable level .####[]
None Researchers have shown that without a determined policy on climate coordinated at international level the consequences of climate change will be dramatic .####[]
None The average global temperature will increase by 5.8d C by 2100 , sea levels will rise by up to 90 cm over the same period , and there will be an increasing number of hurricanes with ever more serious consequences , while man and nature will have to cope with a shift in climate and rainfall zones the like of which has never been seen before .####[]
None At our instigation , on 4 March EU environment ministers therefore called on the United States to " assume its responsibilities under the framework agreement on climate change , " that is to stabilize greenhouse gas emissions at 1990 levels and strengthen domestic actions to bring them into line with the level of effort accepted by the industrial countries in application of the Kyoto Protocol .####[([14, 30], [11, 14], [8, 10], 'Neutral', 'Weak')]
None If the effects of climate change were not so devastating and our action were to be guided by economic competition , we Europeans could welcome the fact that the United States is not committing itself to an ambitious climate protection program , in so far as the technologies in the field of energy efficiency and renewable energy are the technologies of the future .####[([26, 43], [24, 26], [22, 23], 'Positive', 'Average')]
None Anybody who fails to exploit these markets from the outset will remain lagging behind .####[]
None Demand for these technologies is increasing worldwide .####[]
None The " three liters for 100 kilometers " car , high efficiency turbines , and solar panels are export successes and their development is driven by a climate protection policy of growing amplitude .####[]
None Even today it is difficult to find buyers outside the United States for the fuel- guzzling cars of the US automobile industry .####[]
None US reticence is not therefore a reason for us to reduce our climate protection efforts .####[]
None The dominant role of the European climate protection policy has benefits for our economy .####[]
None Many studies show that an active policy of climate protection is not in any way contrary to a policy of full employment .####[]
None On the contrary , it can have a positive effect .####[]
None By implementing our European and national climate protection programs we will succeed in creating several hundred thousand new jobs by 2010 .####[]

None TAIPEI , Sept 27 ( AFP ) -- Taiwan is expected to officially become a full member of the World Trade Organization ( WTO ) in March 2002 , Vice Minister of Economic Affairs Steve Chen said Thursday .####[]
None " March appears to be a more reasonable estimate while earlier admission cannot be entirely ruled out , " according to Chen , also Taiwan 's chief WTO negotiator .####[]
None After having secured the approval of a working panel in Geneva , Taiwan 's entry has yet to be ratified at the WTO 's ministerial meeting set for Qatar in November and then undergo parliamentary deliberation at home , he said .####[]
None Chen said Taiwan is set to reduce the average tariff rate on 1,021 farm products to 12.9 percent after its WTO accession from 20.0 percent currently .####[]
None " We will also phase out internal protection of such products and remove export subsidies . "####[]
None At the same time , the average tariff rate on 3,470 industrial items would be slashed to 4.2 percent eventually from the current 6.0 percent , he added .####[]
None Under a quota system , the tariffs on imported cars would be reduced from 30.0 percent in the first year after Taiwan 's WTO entry to 17.5 percent in 10 years , he said .####[]
None Chen said Taiwan 's external trade has less of a need to readjust itself in the post - WTO era as it has long functioned under a market -oriented economy and already largely conforms to international conventions .####[]
None Taiwan -made products stood a good chance of becoming even more competitive thanks to wider access to overseas markets and lower costs for material imports , he said .####[]
None However an expected increase in farm imports would certainly have an impact on the domestic agricultural sector , he said .####[]
None The vice minister said Taiwan 's service industry was unlikely to sustain an excessive impact as it has been largely opened to private and foreign participation .####[]
None Instead , service ventures in the financial , transport and telecom sectors should benefit from the introduction of advanced skills and expertise from abroad , he added .####[]

None The most frequent crimes involved the loss or theft of Korean passports , according to the official .####[]
None Last year alone , 1,800 Korean passports were reported missing in China -- 1,000 in Shenyang , Liaoning Province , 400 in Beijing and 200 in Shanghai , the official said .####[]
None Missing passports find their way to human traffickers , he said .####[]
None " About 90 percent of foreigners ' missing passports are Korean's , and the missing passports are being used mostly for crimes like illegal entry , downgrading the nation 's credibility in the international community , " the official said .####[]
None The number of crimes committed by Koreans has also been on the increase .####[]
None Among the crimes are illegal trafficking or forgery of passports , drug production and transportation , smuggling , overstaying visas and drunk driving , the official said .####[]
None Last year , 1.6 million Koreans travelled to China , up from 1.34 million in 2000 , and the number of Korean students in China hit 16,000 , more than any other country ; Japan trailed with 15,000 students , the official said .####[]

None The restaurant operator cited transaction costs from its 1988 recapitalization as a result of a $ 160 million restructuring of its bank debt .####[]
None The write - off will be reported as an extraordinary item in the company 's 1989 operating results .####[]
None In addition , the effective interest rate on the $ 410 million of total remaining bank debt after the restructuring is 10.66 % .####[]
None The combined effect of these changes is expected to save the company about $ 4 million in interest expenses next year , or six cents a share .####[]
