None A Brief History Jerusalem ' s recorded history begins with its mention in Egyptian court records 4,000 years ago , but there had been human settlements here for centuries , probably millennia , before that .####[]
None At the beginning of the second millennium b.c. , Jerusalem was a Canaanite mountain stronghold on a secondary trade route , far less important than biblical cities such as Hazor , Megiddo , Beth Shean , and Shechem .####[]
None The earliest name associated with the city , Ur usalim , perhaps meant ``city of Shalim ' ' or ``founded by Shalim .####[]
None '' Scholars speculate that Shalim might have been an ancient Semitic deity of peace , for the name resembles the modern Hebrew and Arabic words for ``peace '' : shalom and salaam , respectively .####[]
None If true , this is an ironic name for a city that would become one of the most constantly and bitterly embattled places on the face of the earth .####[]
None Biblical Jerusalem####[]
None In the Bible , Genesis 14:18 -- 20 records that Abraham visited the city of ` `Salem ' ' in approximately 1800 b.c. and was blessed by the city ' s ruler , Melchzedik , who offered him bread and wine .####[([10, 11], [25, 27], [28, 35], 'Positive', 'Average')]
None The city is not mentioned again in the Bible until the time of the great poet warrior , King David , who captured the city from the Jebusites in about 1000 b.c .####[]
None The Bible describes how David ' s soldiers conquered Jerusalem by discovering a water tunnel under the walls and using it to take the city by surprise .####[]
None Warren ' s Shaft , part of a Canaanite water system discovered by 19th - century archaeologists and open to visitors , might be the very tunnel infiltrated by David ' s army .####[]
None Perhaps because Jerusalem was in neutral territory not allotted to any of the twelve rival tribes of Israel , David made it the capital of his newly formed kingdom and brought the most talented artisans , dedicated priests , magical poets and musicians , and the most formidable soldiers from each of the tribes to live in his city .####[]
None He also brought the Ark of the Covenant , the portable tabernacle containing the Tablets of the Law received on Mount Sinai , to the Spring of Gihon , just outside the walls of Jerusalem .####[]
None There the Ark rested until it was placed in the Temple , built in approximately 960 b.c. on Mt. Moriah , the high point at the northern end of the city .####[]
None The Temple ( today known as the ` `First '' Temple ) was completed by David ' s son and successor , King Solomon .####[]
None According to biblical tradition , although David bought the land for the Temple and carefully assembled its building materials , he was deemed unworthy of constructing the Temple because he was a man of war with blood on his hands .####[([21, 22], [22, 23], [2, 5], 'Neutral', 'Average'), ([0], [22, 23], [2, 5], 'Neutral', 'Average')]
None At the Temple ' s dedication , Solomon addressed his God : ``... the Heavens , even the Heaven of the Heavens , cannot contain####[([0], [8, 10], [7, 8], 'Neutral', 'Average'), ([0], [8, 10], [7, 8], 'Neutral', 'Average')]
None Thee ; how much less this House that I have built ?####[]
None ' '####[]
None The site of the Temple eventually became identified as Mt. Moriah , on which it stood , where Abraham was called to sacrifice his son Isaac .####[([22, 27], [20, 22], [0], 'Positive', 'Weak')]
None Along with this splendid house of worship , Solomon built a royal palace , mansions for his wives , temples for the foreign gods worshipped by the princesses he had married , and towers for the defense of the capital .####[]
None Under the wise reign of Solomon , the city flourished as the capital of an empire that stretched from Damascus to the Red Sea and controlled the trade routes from Egypt to Phoenicia .####[]
None The Temple and royal palace were adorned with gold and ivory from Africa and with cedar from Lebanon ; the beauties and glories of Jerusalem under Solomon have captivated readers of the Bible for almost 3,000 years .####[([20, 28], [28, 29], [29, 34], 'Positive', 'Average')]
None But with his death the empire collapsed , and the Israelite kingdom was divided into two separate , impoverished , often warring nations : Israel , with its capital at Shechem in the north , ruled by a series of northern dynasties ; and the smaller kingdom of Judah , with its capital at Jerusalem , from which the Davidic dynasty continued to rule .####[]
None The Bible tells us that the cruelty and impiety of the rulers of both kingdoms aroused the fury of the great Prophets .####[([11, 15], [3, 5], [1, 2], 'Neutral', 'Average'), ([6, 15], [18, 19], [1, 2], 'Negative', 'Strong')]
None In 701 b.c. the Assyrian armies of Sennacherib destroyed Israel and moved southward to besiege Jerusalem .####[]
None Thanks to King Hezekiah ' s hidden water tunnel , the city narrowly escaped destruction .####[]
None The end of David ' s dynasty came in 587 b.c. , when Nebuchadnezzar , King of Babylon , invaded Judah to lay siege to Jerusalem .####[]
None When it fell , the Temple and all the buildings were burned .####[]
None The people of the once-glorious city were forced into an exile known as ``the Babylonian Captivity .####[]
None ' '####[]
None In time , the kingdom of Babylon was overthrown and the Israelites were permitted to return to Jerusalem in 539 b.c .####[]
None The city was now under the more tolerant rule of the Persians , but rebuilding was slow work .####[]
None The Second Temple was finished in 515 b.c. , but much of the city still lay in ruins .####[]
None Jerusalem submitted peaceably to the rule of the Greeks in 332 b.c. under Alexander the Great and , subsequently , to his Hellenistic successors as well as the Egyptian Ptolomeys and the Syrian Seleucids .####[]
None When Seleucid rulers outlawed Judaism , Jews led by Judah Maccabee and his brothers staged a revolution in 167 b.c. and , against all odds , restored the primacy of Jewish religious life in Jerusalem .####[]
None The Macabbees cleansed the Temple of Hellenistic idols and the blood of pagan sacrifices ; the eight - day celebration of Hanukkah ( Feast of Dedication ) commemorates their victory .####[]
None The Hasmonean dynasty , descendants of the Maccabee family , ruled an independent Jewish Commonwealth that stretched from the Negev to the Galilee .####[]
None Jerusalem grew , surrounded with a formidable wall and defended by towers beside the Jaffa Gate .####[]
None The Hasmoneans ruled until Pompey ' s Roman legions arrived in 63 b.c. Roman Jerusalem####[]
None After the initial years of Roman administration and political infighting , Rome installed Herod ( scion of a family from Idumea , a Jewish kingdom in the desert ) as King of Judea .####[]
None He reigned from 37 to 4 b.c. , during which time he fortified the Hasmonean wall and rebuilt the defense towers beside Jaffa Gate , the foundation of which still stand .####[]
None Several palaces were built and a water system installed .####[]
None Herod also completely rebuilt the Temple , making it one of the most important religious centers in the Roman Empire .####[]
None The courtyard around the Temple was expanded to accommodate hundreds of thousands of pilgrims , and the Temple Mount was shored up by retaining walls made with great stone blocks .####[]
None One of these walls , the Western Wall , is today a major reminder of Jerusalem ' s greatness under Herod .####[]
None A massive fortress was built overlooking the Temple Mount , which Herod named ` `Antonia ' ' in honor of his Roman friend and benefactor , Mark Antony .####[([21, 29], [13, 14], [12], 'Positive', 'Average')]
None For all his accomplishments , Herod was nevertheless hated by his subjects ; he taxed , he tortured , and he ordered the massacre of male Jewish infants in an attempt to do away with the heralded Messiah .####[([6, 7], [9, 10], [11, 14], 'Negative', 'Strong')]
None When Jesus was born in about 4 b.c. , Joseph and Mary escaped Herod ' s paranoia by fleeing into Egypt with the new-born infant .####[([0], [16, 18], [14, 16], 'Negative', 'Average')]
None They returned to live in the Galilee village of Nazareth , making pilgrimages to Jerusalem .####[]
None According to biblical accounts , Jesus spent his life ministering in the Galilee Valley .####[]
None In about a.d. 30 he and his followers went for Passover to Jerusalem , which was in unrest at this time , dissatisfied with Roman domination .####[([25, 27], [22, 24], [12, 14], 'Negative', 'Average')]
None Jesus ' s entry into the Temple caused a commotion ; after the Passover dinner he was arrested by the temple priests , who were under direct Roman rule .####[]
None Jesus was put on trial quickly and condemned to crucifixion , a Roman form of execution for political and religious dissidents as well as for common criminals .####[]
None In a province rife with rebellion and retaliation , the execution in Jerusalem of yet another religious leader from the Galilee did not by itself have an immediate effect on history .####[]
None After Jesus ' s crucifixion , harsh Roman rule continued until a.d. 66 , when the Jews rebelled .####[]
None For four years Jewish zealots fought against the might of Rome .####[]
None At the end , the Roman general Titus laid siege to Jerusalem in a.d. 70 , finally attacking its starved and weakened defenders .####[]
None Those who didn ' t escape were executed or sold into slavery .####[]
None The Holy City and the Temple were destroyed .####[]
None The last of the zealots held out for another three years at Masada ( see page 76 ) .####[]
None Half a million civilians died in the Galilee and Judea as a result of this first revolt against Rome , a number unequaled in ancient warfare .####[]
None Christian and Islamic Jerusalem For 60 years Jerusalem lay in ruins , until the Roman Emperor Hadrian ordered the city rebuilt as a Roman town dedicated to Jupiter .####[]
None In outrage , the Jews began a second revolt against Rome , led by Simon bar Kochba .####[([0], [1, 3], [4, 5], 'Negative', 'Strong')]
None The ruins of Jerusalem were briefly liberated , but , in the end , Jewish resistance to Rome was defeated with great loss of life .####[]
None The planned new Roman city , Aelia Capitolina , was built over the ruins of Herodian Jerusalem , and Jews were barred from residing there for all time .####[]
None Jerusalem ' s physical existence as a spiritual city seemed finished , but its spiritual power for Jews , and for the struggling new Christian religion , remained .####[]
None For the next two centuries Aelia Capitolina enjoyed an innocuous history .####[]
None But the Roman Empire became Christian in the fourth century , and Jerusalem became a center of religion once again .####[]
None Queen Helena , a devout Christian and the mother of Emperor Constantine the Great , made a pilgrimage to the Holy Land in 326 to identify the sites associated with Jesus ' s life .####[([0], [4, 5], [1, 4], 'Positive', 'Strong')]
None She found that the city ' s most beautiful Roman temple , dedicated to the goddess Aphrodite , stood on the site of the crucifixion .####[([10, 12], [2, 3], [1], 'Neutral', 'Average')]
None The temple was demolished and a vast , Classical - style church was built around Golgotha ( the hill where Jesus ' s crucifixion was believed to have taken place ) .####[]
None Throughout Jerusalem , other spots important to Jesus ' s life were commemorated with religious structures .####[]
None Pilgrims came from all over the Roman ( and , later , Byzantine ) Empire during the following centuries , but the prosperity they brought lasted only until 614 , when Persian armies overtook Judea and reduced Jerusalem to rubble again .####[]
None In 629 , Jerusalem was recaptured by the Byzantines .####[]
None Still reeling from the effects of the Persian devastation , Jerusalem was conquered in 638 by the forces of Islam .####[]
None The Temple Mount was identified in Islamic tradition as ` `the farthest spot '' ( in Arabic , el-aksa ) , the site to which the Prophet Muhammad was transported in one night from Mecca on a winged horse , as described in the 17th chapter of the Koran .####[]
None From here the Prophet ascended to the heavens and was permitted to glimpse paradise .####[]
None The rock on the Temple Mount from which he ascended , at or close to the site of the ruined Temple , was commemorated by the construction of the Dome of the Rock in 691 .####[]
None The Dome of the Rock remains Jerusalem ' s most striking monument ; it is counted among the most beautiful buildings ever created .####[([1, 5], [15, 16], [0], 'Neutral', 'Average')]
None By about 715 , the El- Aksa Mosque , third holiest place of prayer in Islam ( after Mecca and Medina ) , had been built on the southern side of the Temple Mount .####[]
None Jerusalem continued under Islamic rule for the next four and a half centuries .####[]
None In 1099 , under their leaders Godfrey de Bouillon and Tancred , the Crusaders captured the Holy City for Christendom by slaughtering both Muslims and Jews .####[]
None Crusaders , Mamelukes , and Turks####[]
None The Crusaders established a feudal Christian state with Godfrey at its head .####[]
None They built many impressive churches during the term of the first Latin Kingdom of Jerusalem , but in 1187 they were driven out by Muslim forces under the great warrior Saladin .####[]
None During the Sixth Crusade ( 1228 -- 1229 ) , the Holy Roman Emperor Frederick II managed to secure Jerusalem for the Christians by negotiation .####[]
None The Christians , however , could not hold the city .####[]
None After they lost Jerusalem , a Mongol invasion swept through , and in 1244 the Mameluke dynasty of Egypt took control , ruling Jerusalem for the next 250 years .####[]
None The city struggled to rebuild from Crusader wars and invasions .####[]
None Much of the best Islamic architecture in the city was constructed in the Mameluke era , but the past thousand years had taken their toll : Jerusalem was unable to regain the prosperity it had enjoyed in earlier times .####[]
None In the early 16th century , the Ottoman Turkish Empire was advancing through the Middle East .####[]
None Jerusalem fell to the Ottomans in 1517 , remaining under their control for 400 years .####[]
None Suleiman the Magnificent rebuilt the walls and gates in the form they retain to this day .####[]
None Fountains , inns , religious schools , and barracks were constructed .####[]
None But when Suleiman died , his empire , including Jerusalem , began a long period of decline .####[]
None The Holy City remained a backwater until the 19th century , when renewed interest among Christian pilgrims made it the destination of thousands of travelers each year .####[([1, 3], [12, 14], [15, 18], 'Positive', 'Average')]
None 19th -Century Aspirations####[]
None At the same time , many Jews sought religious freedom and fulfillment by moving to Palestine ( as the Holy Land was traditionally called ) and especially to Jerusalem .####[([8, 11], [7, 8], [7], 'Positive', 'Average')]

None The problem was that British strategists , who were fighting the Ottoman Turks in 1917 , had secretly promised the lands to their World War I Arab allies .####[]
None In 1922 the League of Nations granted the British a mandate to administer Palestine .####[]
None Jerusalem flourished during the early years of the Mandate .####[]
None Modern neighborhoods , hospitals , schools , and the Hebrew University were built in West Jerusalem , the new Jewish enclave .####[]
None But Arab opposition to new Jewish immigration and construction in Palestine led to increasing strife ; by 1946 , Jerusalem was an armed camp .####[([5, 12], [2, 4], [2], 'Negative', 'Average')]
None In 1947 the United Nations voted for the partition of Palestine into two states , one Jewish and one Arab , with Jerusalem as an international city that belonged to neither .####[]
None But lacking the means to enforce its decision , the United Nations was powerless to halt the fighting that erupted as the British withdrew their troops in 1948 .####[]

None The State of Israel was declared during this difficult time .####[]
None In response , member states of the Arab League sent troops to help the Palestinian Arabs .####[]

None Free access to holy sites for members of all religions was guaranteed by the armistice agreements .####[]

None BETHANY - The number of illegal immigrants in Swaziland seems to be increasing .####[]
None Last month members of the Umbutfo Swaziland Defence Force [ USDF ] found 594 illegal aliens in the country .####[]
None The USDF found 43 Somalians inside two kombis in Maphiveni and 23 others were found without travel documents at Matsamo border and were handed over to the Horo police .####[]
None At least 507 illegal Mozambicans have been found , as well as eight South Africans , two Tanzanians , and one Burundian .####[]
None According to the army spokesman , Corporal Nhlanhla Dlamini , the key areas where most of the immigrants were found was Lomahasha , Mhlumeni and Sitsatsaweni .####[]
None " We have discovered that there is a certain family around Lomahasha , which is suspected of assisting illegal immigrants with shelter and transport .####[]
None The army would like to request whoever is engaged in this criminal activity , to stop , " he said .####[([6, 15], [3, 6], [19, 20], 'Positive', 'Average'), ([6, 18], [3, 6], [19, 20], 'Positive', 'Average')]
None Last month , 53 cattle were also stolen around the country , of which 17 were spotted inside Mozambique driven by three men armed with rifles thought to be AK47s .####[]
None The Mozambican soldiers have promised to act quickly .####[]
None The USDF also found four stolen cars in different places in the country .####[]
None These include a Nissan Skyline in Mafutseni , a Mercedes Benz , A Toyota and an Isuzu 2.5 diesel at Nkalashane .####[]
